A burning skeleton arrives from above.
The Courthouse
The open shell of this building is all that remains of the former
courthouse. The ceiling has long since caved in, leaving the interior of
the building exposed to the environment. The attached jail cells have been
crushed by the building, but you see no signs of their former occupants.
Most likely they fled during the chaos of whatever ravaged this city.
A burning skeleton stands before you.

Northern Road
The stone tiles of this road have long since lost their form and

leads eastward towards the market.

413H 148V 10196673X 1173C Mem:2 Exits:NES>
n
A burning skeleton arrives from the south.
North Gate
The northern gate of Tarsis once stood as an inpenetrable boundary to
would-be attackers from the Plains of Dust. Guards would patrol this area
and often and protected the cities inhabitants from the nomads and common
criminals that dwelled within the Plains. Now the shattered gate stands as
an eternal testament to their failure: the gate itself has long been torn
out of its frame and shattered onto the stone road of the city.
A burning skeleton stands before you.

A burning skeleton arrives from the east.
The Northern Park Entrance
Twisted, crushed iron, painted in rust, is all that remains of the
fence and gate that used to separate the park from the city. The grass that
once bordered the path into the park has been replaced by dust while the
path itself has been broken by weeds.
A burning skeleton stands before you.

Before the Library
Two large wooden double doors in the southern wall once opened to
scholars seeking the knowledge and wisdom that was housed within the Great
Tarsis Library. Now only a single, beaten door remains, barely hanging from
its rusted hinges, threatening to fall and shatter itself on the stone
floor. The wall to the north is a crumbling testament to the power of time
and neglect: what was once relied upon to protect the city from invaders is
little more than a mound of stones that a small child could surmount.

containing knowledge of the arcane arts, history, science, mathematics and
countless other subjects. Now all of that is lost. Whatever was not
crushed, burned or otherwise destroyed has long since turned to dust. The
countless shelves that were once lined with books are nowhere to be seen
amidst the rubble.

Before the Library
Two large wooden double doors in the southern wall once opened to

North Gate
The northern gate of Tarsis once stood as an inpenetrable boundary to
would-be attackers from the Plains of Dust. Guards would patrol this area
and often and protected the cities inhabitants from the nomads and common
criminals that dwelled within the Plains. Now the shattered gate stands as
an eternal testament to their failure: the gate itself has long been torn
out of its frame and shattered onto the stone road of the city.

Wall Road
Once there was an immense lookout tower at the northeast corner of
Tarsis that provided city guards with a vantage point to survey the
surrounding landscape. That tower collapsed inward, into the city, bringing

leading south into the market, and west towards the northern gate.

The Ruined Market
Large, burned out craters speckle the marketplace here serving as an
indication as to what happened to this mighty city. It is likely this area
was heavily targetted when the city was attacked because of the dense
population of a crowded marketplace. The surrounding buildings are hollowed
shells of their former glory: walls are filled with large holes, roofs have
collapsed into several of the buildings, entryways have filled with rubble.

East Gate
All that remains of this once great gate are splinters of wood and
broken stone. Portions of the archway that once framed the gate have
collapsed and there are gaping holes in the thick city walls. These gates
once repelled swarms of attackers, but the slow decay of time has broken it
down. The path that once lead to the southeastern portion of town ends in a
sudden drop-off; only a gaping crater remains where the buildings once
stood tall.

The Tarsis Dump
A forsaken desert surrounds you, swallows you whole with its forceful
gales that hurl grains of sand deep into your skin. It is as if the wind is
penetrating your bones. Scattered pieces of brick and stone have been
discarded here in the dump. Where once a steady stream of horse-drawn cart
would carry the refuse of tarsis to this forsaken landfill, nothing stirs.
There is little here that is still useful, but the ancient bones of what
you can assume were vagrants lie amidst the trash, with the hopes of their
once peaceful lives covered with filth.
